<td colspan="2" style="text-align: left">
<p><i>Aquila rapax nipalensis</i>
</p>
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>The <b> steppe eagle</b> (<i>Aquila nipalensis</i>) is a large <a href="/wiki/Bird_of_prey" title="Bird of prey">bird of prey</a>. Like all <a href="/wiki/Eagle" title="Eagle">eagles</a>, it belongs to the family <a href="/wiki/Accipitridae" title="Accipitridae">Accipitridae</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle's well-feathered legs illustrate it to be a member of the subfamily <a href="/wiki/Aquilinae" title="Aquilinae">Aquilinae</a>, also known as the "booted eagles".<sup id="cite_ref-Helbig_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Helbig-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> This species was once considered to be closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">non-migratory</a> <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">tawny eagle</a> (<i>Aquila rapax</i>) and the two forms have previously been treated as <a href="/wiki/Biological_specificity" title="Biological specificity">conspecific</a>. They were split based on pronounced differences in morphology and anatomy;<sup id="cite_ref-Clark_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Olson_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> two molecular studies, each based on a very small number of genes, indicate that the species are distinct but disagree over how closely related they are.<sup id="cite_ref-Olson_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-globalraptors_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalraptors-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sangster_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangster-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The steppe eagle is in many ways a peculiar species of eagle. It is a specialized predator of <a href="/wiki/Ground_squirrel" title="Ground squirrel">ground squirrels</a> on the breeding ground, also taking other rather small <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> and other prey, doing so more often when ground squirrels are less consistently found.<sup id="cite_ref-Vazhov_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vazhov-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In rather treeless areas of the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> habitats, these eagles tend to nest on a slightly rise, often on or near an <a href="/wiki/Outcrop" title="Outcrop">outcrop</a>, but may even the flat, wide-open ground, in a rather flat nest. They are the only eagle to nest primarily on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Usually one to three eggs are laid and, in successful nests, one to two young eagles fledge.<sup id="cite_ref-Karyakin_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karyakin-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle undertakes a massive migration from essentially its entire breeding range, moving en masse past major migration flyways, especially those of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In winter, though less closely studied than during breeding, the steppe eagle is remarkable for its sluggish and almost passive feeding ecology, focusing on <a href="/wiki/Insect" title="Insect">insect</a> <a href="/wiki/Swarm_behaviour" title="Swarm behaviour">swarms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carrion" title="Carrion">carrion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Altriciality" title="Altriciality">semi-altricial young</a> of assorted animals, lacking the bold and predatory demeanor of their cousin species.<sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Although still seen by the thousands at migration sites in larger numbers than other migrating eagles of these areas, the steppe eagle's entire population has declined precipitously.<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The threats to this species consist of increasing <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">steppe fires</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a> around the nests (both probably increased by the <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">warming climate</a>) which can cause a large volume of nest failures. Rivaling these factors, disturbance and persecution by humans and trampling by <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> are also destroying many nests. Free-flying steppe eagles are also being killed in alarmingly large numbers, especially in the stronghold nation for breeding of <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Electrocution" title="Electrocution">electrocutions</a> on dangerous <a href="/wiki/Electrical_wiring" title="Electrical wiring">electricial wires</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transmission_tower" title="Transmission tower">pylons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Karyakin9_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karyakin9-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Due to these and other reasons, the decline of the species is thought to be considerably in excess of 50%. Therefore, the species is considered to be <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered</a> by the <a href="/wiki/IUCN" class="mw-redirect" title="IUCN">IUCN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The Steppe Eagle appears on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Kazakhstan" title="Flag of Kazakhstan">flag of Kazakhstan</a>. It is also the national bird (animal) of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and appears on its flag.
</p>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomy">Taxonomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Taxonomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>British naturalist <a href="/wiki/Brian_Houghton_Hodgson" title="Brian Houghton Hodgson">Brian Houghton Hodgson</a> described the steppe eagle in 1833. <i>Aquila</i> is <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "eagle" while <i>nipalensis</i> means "from <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>" based on the location where the <a href="/wiki/Type_(biology)" title="Type (biology)">type specimen</a> was collected presumably while migrating.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Aquilinae" title="Aquilinae">booted eagle</a> subfamily within the <a href="/wiki/Accipitridae" title="Accipitridae">Accipitridae</a> family.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The booted eagle clan are <a href="/wiki/Monophyly" title="Monophyly">monophyletic</a> and study of <a href="/wiki/Karyotype" title="Karyotype">karyotypes</a> has indicated that they likely have few to no close external relations within the overall extant accipitrid family.<sup id="cite_ref-Helbig_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Helbig-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The booted eagle subfamily all have feathers covering their legs and may be found to some extent on every continent that contains accipitrids.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The genus <i>Aquila</i> is has been thought to traditionally composed of by large and fairly dark eagles that generally habituate to various open habitats. However, a significant division was determined to exist between superficially similar eagles such as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a> (<i>Aquila chrysaetos</i>) and its three extant and similar-looking close cousins, as well as three very different smaller and pale-bellied eagles, and the <a href="/wiki/Species_complex" title="Species complex">species complex</a> which contains the steppe eagle.<sup id="cite_ref-Helbig_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Helbig-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lerner_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Watson_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> There is a similar genetic disparity with the golden eagle for the steppe eagle as with the <a href="/wiki/Clanga_(genus)" title="Clanga (genus)">spotted eagles</a> which have been deemed distinct enough to form a separate genus, <i>Clanga</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Valli_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valli-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle genetically clusters closely to the <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">tawny eagle</a> as well as, albeit more distantly, with the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle" title="Eastern imperial eagle">eastern</a> (<i>Aquila heliaca</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_imperial_eagle" title="Spanish imperial eagle">Spanish imperial eagles</a> (<i>Aquila adalberti</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Lerner_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lerner-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zhou_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zhou-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Locus_(genetics)" title="Locus (genetics)">loci</a> evidenced in the <i>Aquila</i> genera have been found to be relatively homogenous, with general studies of <a href="/wiki/Isoenzyme" class="mw-redirect" title="Isoenzyme">isoenzymes</a> showing their genes as about ten times less distanced than certain <a href="/wiki/Asio" title="Asio">owl</a> genera.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The steppe eagle has historically been considered conspecific with the tawny eagle, even until as recently as 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amadon_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amadon-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The latter species resides year-round in the African and Asian areas often used seasonally as wintering grounds by steppe eagle.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The species were ultimately separated on the grounds of the differences in morphology, disparate coloring, distinct life histories and behaviours.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Olson_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sangster_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sangster-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark2_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Testing of genetic materials has reinforced the species distinction of the steppe and tawny eagles. Genetically, the steppe eagle is thought to be <a href="/wiki/Basal_(phylogenetics)" title="Basal (phylogenetics)">basal</a> to related species such as the tawny and imperial eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-Olson_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A fossil species, <i>Aquila nipaloides</i>, has been found in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and was hypothesized to most closely related to the steppe eagle based on <a href="/wiki/Osteology" title="Osteology">osteology</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Mandible" title="Mandible">ramus</a> (although did evidence some differences in leg morphology).<sup id="cite_ref-Louchart_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Louchart-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Despite being even more strongly distinctive from the steppe eagle than the tawny eagle, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle" title="Eastern imperial eagle">eastern imperial eagle</a> has been seen to <a href="/wiki/Hybridisation_(biology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybridisation (biology)">hybridize</a> with the steppe eagles in the wild, once in <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkey (country)">Turkey</a> and at least three times in Kazakhstan. Each hybrid with imperial eagles has been known to involve pairs of subadult or juvenile eagles and all known hybrid pairings were between male steppe eagles (or apparent steppe-imperial hybrids themselves) mated to female imperial eagles. Some of these hybrid pairs also produced seemingly healthy young with roughly intermediate characteristics.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The steppe eagle has been generally considered to contain two subspecies. One was the nominate subspecies, <i>A. n. nipalensis</i>, which breeds in the eastern portions of the range (perhaps from the <a href="/wiki/East_Kazakhstan_Region" title="East Kazakhstan Region">East Kazakhstan Region</a> to all points east) while the western breeding population, found in most of Kazakhstan and <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a>, was considered as the subspecies, <i>A. n. orientalis</i>. The separation of two subspecies was largely based on size, with the eastern population being larger and much heavier than the western eagles. The more eastern birds tend to be a shade darker and a have a more extensive nape patch, as well as having a more conspicuously deep gape-line.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> However, both western and Russian researchers have since made a convincing advocacy that the steppe eagle is actually a <a href="/wiki/Monotypic_taxon" title="Monotypic taxon">monotypical species</a>. It was found that both previously claimed subspecies appear to broadly overlap in the breeding range and become indistinguishable at the Kazakh-Russian meeting point. The primary differences, i.e. in size and mildly in colour, can be explained as <a href="/wiki/Cline_(biology)" title="Cline (biology)">clinal variations</a> due to the environment. The breeding populations of the eastern and western eagles are insufficiently <a href="/wiki/Allopatric_speciation" title="Allopatric speciation">allopatric</a> and too extensively engage in <a href="/wiki/Introgression" title="Introgression">introgression</a> to be properly regarded as full subspecies.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-globalraptors_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalraptors-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Subspecies_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subspecies-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Erroneously, a checklist once included the former subspecies of <i>A. n. orientalis</i> as being part of the subspecies of tawny eagle from Asia, <i>A. r. vindhiana</i>, an error that was later corrected.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg/220px-Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg/330px-Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg/440px-Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle%27s_Gape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The gape of the steppe eagle is an easy way to distinguish it from the tawny eagle. The gape extends beyond the centre of the eye as against the tawny. The oval nostril sets it apart from the spotted eagles.</div></div></div>
<p>The steppe eagle is a large, bulky and robust-looking eagle. It is mainly dark brown in colour with a longish but very thick neck and a relatively small head that nonetheless features a strong <a href="/wiki/Beak" title="Beak">bill</a> and long gape-line. It appears long-winged and has a longish and rather rounded tail and markedly well-feathered (almost with disheveled looking feathers) legs. Steppe eagles tend to perch somewhat upright and usually do so in the open, often utilizing isolated <a href="/wiki/Tree" title="Tree">trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utility_pole" title="Utility pole">posts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">rocks</a> or other suitable low lookouts such as <a href="/wiki/Mound" title="Mound">mounds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Straw" title="Straw">straw-piles</a>. The species often is seen on the ground where may stand for long periods of the day and walk with horizontal posture and with wingtips just exceed the tail-tip. Steppe eagles, like tawny eagles, can fairly tame and approachable, unlike many of the other <i>Aquila</i> eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The adult is a somewhat variable brown with darker centers to the <a href="/wiki/Covert_feather" title="Covert feather">greater coverts</a>. More pronouncedly in the eastern part of the range, adults have normally prominent pale rufous to dull orange-yellow to yellow-brown patches on the nape and hindcrown.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dementiev_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dementiev-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Any other paler areas (such as the feather tips of the back and uppertail coverts) are obscured on perched adults. The massive gape-line runs to level with the rear of eye (further emphasized by dark border against paler chin) and is longer than in any other <i>Aquila</i> eagles including tawny eagles. Combined with their deep-set eyes, it lends steppe eagles an altogether rather fierce facial expression.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Steppe eagle juveniles are almost invariably paler than adults, with some ranging overall from <a href="/wiki/Umber" title="Umber">umber</a>-brown to <a href="/wiki/Tawny_(color)" title="Tawny (color)">tawny</a>-<a href="/wiki/Buff_(colour)" title="Buff (colour)">buff</a> but then some are darker and more deeply brown.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark3_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Juveniles tend to be brown to grey-brown on the upperparts but for generally rufous-buff nape patch (more so on eastern population).<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The juveniles bear conspicuously and broadly white-tipped black about the greater coverts, wings and tail and a bold but narrow cream band on the brown medians. The juvenile steppe eagle's white uppertail coverts is generally concealed when perched; the underparts are usually the same as the upperparts but may be somewhat paler tawny-buff hue. Upon their 2nd year, the plumage is still much as the 1st year appearance but show the pale tips to secondaries, median coverts and tail as often well-worn and narrower; by the start of 2nd winter the, tips of retained juvenile flight-feathers and coverts are heavily abraded and very thin. By the end of 2nd winter, often the immatures look very worn and have nearly lost pale tips altogether and from 3rd year onward manifest a variable mix of old and new feathers. Generally, immatures are often rather scruffy in appearance until adult-like plumage attained at year five, after which the feathers generally appear more compact. Adults have brown to hazel eyes, while juveniles have distinctly dark brown eyes; the cere and feet are yellow at all ages.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis)_(24890757897).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2824890757897%29.jpg/220px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2824890757897%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2824890757897%29.jpg/330px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2824890757897%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2824890757897%29.jpg/440px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2824890757897%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis)_(24890757897).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detailed view of a young steppe eagle in flight in Pakistan.</div></div></div>
<p>In flight, the steppe eagle appears as a large, impressive and visibly heavy raptor with a well-projecting large head and bill and rather broad neck and long, broad wings. They evidence proportionately long arms, especially in the larger eastern birds. The wings tend to be held almost parallel-edged and square-ended with 7 very elongated emarginations. Often juveniles can tend to appear somewhat narrower winged. The broad body of the species often looks suspended underneath and the tail appears rounded or even wedge-shaped, measuring about 3/4 of the length of wing-base. The wingspan is about 2.6 times greater than the total body length.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> On the upperwings, steppe eagles show a pale greyish primary patch that is often quite large and obvious (especially on non-adults), often being pale at the base on the greater primary coverts but on adults (especially dark birds) much less marked. On the underwing, a very small carpal crescent may be present but can vary from invisible to slightly more marked. The <a href="/wiki/Flight_feather" title="Flight feather">flight feathers</a> are greyish and all have 7–8 well-spaced blackish bars (albeit less conspicuously than on spotted eagles), while the fingers are plain blackish. Adults are basically all fairly uniform dark brown (wings can be negligibly greyer or rarely yellowish brown). Adults may evidence in flight some whitish patches on back and tail coverts that are varying from insignificant to fairly prominent. Adult eagles that do show a dark-barred greyish primary patch usually have that confined to a wedge-shape on inner primaries though can sometimes be rather more prominent. Below adults show dark-barred grey flight feathers and tail with the broad blackish trail edges and wing ends being rather distinctive; the wing linings are often slightly paler to darker than remiges and often with an obscure remnant of broken paler central band.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark3_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Juveniles are quite distinctive in flight if seen in reasonable view. Above, juveniles are pale greyish-brown to yellow-brown about the body and forewing-coverts, have a broad whitish U above the tail. They possess broad white tips to the blackish greater coverts, flights feathers and tail creating obvious whitish bars on the wings and trailing edges as well as a large and prominent whitish patch covering much of the inner primaries (causing barring to stand out more so and offsetting plain black wing end). On its underside, the juvenile is mid-brown to brownish-yellow with a paler throat and creamy crissum. Below, the creamy central wing band is even broader than above, while the greater coverts all white with some dark centres on primaries (rare extreme pale individuals appear to have almost uniform paler colour on the entire wing lining and lesser and medians buffish-white to pale sandy, often whitish pale primary-wedges).<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark3_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Despite reports that some juvenile 1st years have subtle or no central wing bands, these are believed to be cases where these feathers exist but are obscured by long median coverts.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark3_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the first year, the young steppe eagle tends to have pale tips to wings, tail and upperwing coverts become rather abraded; thereafter the development young evidence much variation due to individual differences. Usually, by the end of 2nd winter, the wing looks even more worn and uneven in pattern, with any newly acquired narrowly white-tipped quills clearly longer than old worn juvenile ones that have lost their pale tips. From the 3rd winter on, the pale parts clearly reduced, flight feathers and tail often appear quite ragged and by the 4th year start to more resemble adults. From the end of the 3rd year to when they obtain adult plumage, the eagles tend to have adult-like broad blackish trailing edges and tail often coupled with dark-barred grey base to black fingers and traces of the pale band along greater underwing-coverts.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark3_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Maturity is obtained between the 4th and 5th years, not at 6–7 years as previously reported despite some presumed five-year-old eagles still have flecks of pale on the wing coverts and the throat and more subtle nape patches than they will ultimately manifest.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark3_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark3-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark4_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark4-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg/220px-Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg/330px-Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg/440px-Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3513" data-file-height="2333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aravalli_BiodivPark_Gurgaon_DSC9208_steppe_eagle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adult steppe eagle in flight, Aravalli Biodiversity Park, Gurgaon</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Size">Size</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Size">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The steppe eagle is large and impressive raptor and quite a large <a href="/wiki/Eagle" title="Eagle">eagle</a>. However, as a member of the genus <i>Aquila</i>, it is fairly medium-sized.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CRC_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRC-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Females can range to 15% larger with greater <a href="/wiki/Sexual_dimorphism" title="Sexual dimorphism">dimorphism</a> by weight, which is more pronouncedly dimorphic than by linear dimensions.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Total length can range from 60 to 89&#160;cm (24 to 35&#160;in) in fully-grown steppe eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beaman_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beaman-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Wingspan in full grown eagles of this species is very variable, with the smallest steppe eagles spanning as little as 165 to 174&#160;cm (5&#160;ft 5&#160;in to 5&#160;ft 9&#160;in) while the largest ones can reportedly span up to 250 to 262&#160;cm (8&#160;ft 2&#160;in to 8&#160;ft 7&#160;in). Although some sources list the maximum wingspan as only 214 or 216&#160;cm (7&#160;ft 0&#160;in or 7&#160;ft 1&#160;in), the maximum wing dimensions were apparently confirmed for the most massive steppe eagles (i.e. from <a href="/wiki/Altai_Mountains" title="Altai Mountains">Altai</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beaman_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beaman-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Christensen1_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christensen1-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grimmett_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grimmett-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Account_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Account-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Body mass, like wingspan, as reported is also fairly variable. Steppe eagles weighed for a Russia handbook were found to scale from 2.5 to 3.5&#160;kg (5.5 to 7.7&#160;lb) in males while in females weights reported to range from 2.3 to 4.9&#160;kg (5.1 to 10.8&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-Dementiev_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dementiev-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Elsewhere, the minimum full-grown weights for smaller western eagles (formerly subspecies <i>A. n. orientalis</i>) were 2&#160;kg (4.4&#160;lb) for the smallest males while the heaviest females were found to have attained a weight around 3.9&#160;kg (8.6&#160;lb), while weights in the eastern part of the breeding range are around 20% heavier.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In one sample of steppe eagles of possibly varied origins, males weighed a mean of 2.48&#160;kg (5.5&#160;lb) and females a mean of 3.56&#160;kg (7.8&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-Kirmse_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirmse-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Wintering eagles of the species in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">southern Africa</a> weighed a mean of 3.02&#160;kg (6.7&#160;lb) in a sample of four.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, 21 steppe eagles at one study site weighed a mean of 3.28&#160;kg (7.2&#160;lb) while 27 eagles at another study site there weighed a mean of 3.45&#160;kg (7.6&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-Ostrowski_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ostrowski-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Unpublished weights from Israel were much lower at a reported mean of 2.11&#160;kg (4.7&#160;lb), as in other raptors during passage migration in Israel, weight loss may be significant relative to the other seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss2_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss2-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Steppe eagles diagnosed as from the smaller-bodied, western part of the breeding range weighed a mean of 2.46&#160;kg (5.4&#160;lb) in 13 males and a mean of just under 3&#160;kg (6.6&#160;lb) in a sample of 18 females while the mean weight of larger, eastern breeding bird was listed as 3.01&#160;kg (6.6&#160;lb) in 2 males and 3.57&#160;kg (7.9&#160;lb) in 2 females.<sup id="cite_ref-Louchart_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Louchart-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The maximum cited weight for steppe eagle males in the wild is 4.6&#160;kg (10&#160;lb) while that for females is 5.5&#160;kg (12&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-Account_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Account-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Among standard measurements, the <a href="/wiki/Wing_chord_(biology)" title="Wing chord (biology)">wing chord</a> can measure from 510 to 610&#160;mm (20 to 24&#160;in) in males and from 536 to 640&#160;mm (21.1 to 25.2&#160;in) in females. The tail may measure from 238 to 295&#160;mm (9.4 to 11.6&#160;in) in both sexes and the tarsus may be from 85 to 96&#160;mm (3.3 to 3.8&#160;in) in males and from 92 to 98&#160;mm (3.6 to 3.9&#160;in) in females.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Wing chord length averaged 536&#160;mm (21.1&#160;in) and 566&#160;mm (22.3&#160;in) in males and females in a study, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Kirmse_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirmse-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The huge gape of a steppe eagle is from 49 to 60.8&#160;mm (1.93 to 2.39&#160;in) wide, with an average of 53.1 and 55.3&#160;mm (2.09 and 2.18&#160;in) in males and females, respectively, while the gape length is 40 to 49.7&#160;mm (1.57 to 1.96&#160;in), averaging 44.3 and 45.8&#160;mm (1.74 and 1.80&#160;in) in the two sexes.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Claw" title="Claw">hallux claw</a>, the enlarged killing talon on the rear foot of essentially all <a href="/wiki/Accipitridae" title="Accipitridae">accipitrids</a> measures from 28.3 to 36.8&#160;mm (1.11 to 1.45&#160;in), averaging 33.8&#160;mm (1.33&#160;in), in males from 31.8 to 40.5&#160;mm (1.25 to 1.59&#160;in), averaging 36&#160;mm (1.4&#160;in), in females.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Confusion_species">Confusion species</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Confusion species">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG/220px-Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG/330px-Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG/440px-Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="2554" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aquila_nipalensis_2010.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A young captive steppe eagle in Wildpark Tripsdrill, Germany, displaying several typical features including the distinctive pale bands about the wings and huge gape.</div></div></div>
<p>In many circumstances, the steppe eagle can be very difficult to distinguish from other similar eagles, often especially during passage and winter.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Adults are often confused with <a href="/wiki/Clanga_(genus)" title="Clanga (genus)">spotted eagles</a> but are best separated by their much more broad build, far greater wing areas with longer, more rectangular or squarish wing tips and longer, more conspicuous fingers, larger head (rather than small and bull-headed) and larger overall size.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Compared to the spotted eagles, the flight of the steppe eagle is more aquiline, i.e. more powerful, labored and deep while spotted eagles tend to fly more like <a href="/wiki/Buteo" title="Buteo">buzzards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forsman_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lesser_spotted_eagle" title="Lesser spotted eagle">lesser spotted eagle</a> (<i>Clanga pomarina</i>), the most similarly marked of spotted eagles, is particularly less powerful looking with a shorter neck, much smaller wing areas, shorter fingers and tail and less extensive, baggy leg-feathering. The <a href="/wiki/Greater_spotted_eagle" title="Greater spotted eagle">greater spotted eagle</a> (<i>Clanga clanga</i>) is also smaller and slighter but to a reduced extent. When plumage is clear to see, steppe eagles have more clearly and more extensively barred quills and lack the clear carpal arcs of the two widespread spotted eagles but these differences are obscured at greater distances.  Some subadult steppe eagles, with their paler brown wing-coverts above and below and only traces of white underwing bands and clearly pale primary patch above in particular quite resemble the plumage of older lesser spotted eagles. The white wing bars of steppe eagles are usually more conspicuous than those of the lesser spotted eagle.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman2_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alexander_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexander-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> At close range, the steppe eagle has a deeper gape than lesser and greater spotted eagles and has rounded rather than oval nostrils.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman2_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> When seen perched, either on a perch or on the ground, spotted eagles of all three species tend to stand quite tall and upright, emphasizing their more slender and lightly feathered legs, while the steppe eagle sits more horizontally and is always far bulkier than even the biggest greater spotted eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-Forsman_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman2_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Some particularly dark adult and subadult steppe eagles with obscured paler wing feathers can greatly resemble adult greater spotted eagles (the latter species can appear almost blackish in certain lights) and would need to be identified by the differences in size and form.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman2_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman2-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Indian_spotted_eagle" title="Indian spotted eagle">Indian spotted eagle</a> (<i>Clanga hastata</i>) has a deep gape reminiscent of the steppe eagle but is much slighter in overall size, being scarcely larger than a lesser spotted eagle, and has even less conspicuous whitish wing markings than the lesser spotted.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> As a result of their rough similarities, many young steppe eagles are misidentified, particularly from a distance, with spotted eagles although generally, identification is possible via a combination of structure and plumage features.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Juvenile steppe eagles are normally readily identified by distinctive plumage features but can recall juvenile <a href="/wiki/Eastern_imperial_eagle" title="Eastern imperial eagle">eastern imperial eagles</a>, the latter has longer and less rounded tail, a more prominent (rather than deeply set) bill, has a much paler and more buff overall colour while the chest is overlap with brown streaking and the quills are unbarred. Imperial and steppe eagles are often similar in size, with more western breeding birds usually being somewhat smaller when seen side by side with an imperial eagle and the eastern steppe eagles being of similar average size (but even larger maximum size) compared to full-grown imperial eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Christensen1_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christensen1-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Steppe eagles are told from <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">tawny eagles</a> by that species being smaller and less bulky with shorter wings, a smaller gape, a more slender neck and a relatively longer tail. Both the tawny and steppe eagle tend to have a distinct S-shape curvature to the trailing edge of the wings. When perched on the ground, the tawny eagle tends to stand more upright, while the steppe eagle often appears to assume a more elongated, horizontal posture. <a href="/wiki/Polymorphism_(biology)" title="Polymorphism (biology)">Plumage variations</a> of tawny eagles can render them a surprisingly close colour to the usually darker, duller and browner steppe eagle (especially so in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">south Asia</a>), but they never obtain the distinct whitish wing band of the young steppe eagle nor the nape patch of most adult steppes.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clark_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsman_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsman-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Despite slight individual and clinal variations, the steppe eagle, unlike the tawny eagle, is not polymorphic.<sup id="cite_ref-Clark2_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark2-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> These aforementioned eagles present the main possibilities for confusion, less likely mistakes can potentially range from relatively dainty and much smaller <a href="/wiki/Wahlberg%27s_eagle" title="Wahlberg&#39;s eagle">Wahlberg's eagles</a> (<i>Hieraeetus wahlbergi</i>) (generally quite different in features but somewhat similarly hued) in Africa to the somewhat bigger but differently structured <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagles</a> (much longer tail, relatively smaller bill and much smaller gape, different wing shape, more aquiline build and bigger feet and talons) in much of the range.<sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Range_and_habitat">Range and habitat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Range and habitat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breeding_and_wintering_ranges">Breeding and wintering ranges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Breeding and wintering ranges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis)_(33613515334).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2833613515334%29.jpg/220px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2833613515334%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2833613515334%29.jpg/330px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2833613515334%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2833613515334%29.jpg/440px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2833613515334%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis)_(33613515334).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A steppe eagle flying over the snowy mountains near the <a href="/wiki/Hunza_Valley" title="Hunza Valley">Hunza Valley</a> in Pakistan.</div></div></div>
<p>The steppe eagle once bred in Europe. Here, they bred into the 20th century in southeasternmost <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and still rarely occurs as a breeder in <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">southwest Russia</a> from <a href="/wiki/Stavropol_Krai" title="Stavropol Krai">Stavropol</a> to <a href="/wiki/Astrakhan_Oblast" title="Astrakhan Oblast">Astrakhan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle is still mapped to breed down to <a href="/wiki/Makhachkala" title="Makhachkala">Makhachkala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maykop" title="Maykop">Maykop</a> to as far west as <a href="/wiki/Leningradskaya_(rural_locality)" title="Leningradskaya (rural locality)">Leningradskaya</a>, up north as far as the <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">lower Volga</a> and down to the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> nearly as far as <a href="/wiki/Makhachkala" title="Makhachkala">Makhachkala</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/Fort-Shevchenko" title="Fort-Shevchenko">Fort-Shevchenko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The breeding range can extend through appropriate habitat in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> and in much of <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, from north of <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a> south to (albeit spottily) to <a href="/wiki/Kyzylorda_Region" title="Kyzylorda Region">Kyzylorda</a> as well as around the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>, sweeping far to the east in <a href="/wiki/Transbaikal" title="Transbaikal">Transbaikal</a> and western <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altai_Mountains" title="Altai Mountains">Altai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gansu" title="Gansu">Gansu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ningxia" title="Ningxia">Ningxia</a>, northern <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> (by far their southernmost breeding area), <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a> and reaching their eastern breeding limits in <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> and elsewhere in <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Northeastern China">northeastern China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle is entirely migratory, wintering in <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">east</a> and, to a lesser extent, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">southern Africa</a>. Their African range can extend western to southern <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, almost throughout <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">east Africa</a>, to the easternmost part of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The southern African wintering range extends to central <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, northern and eastern <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> south to <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, including former <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Transvaal Province">Transvaal</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Natal_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Natal (region)">Natal</a> as well as rarely south of the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River" title="Orange River">Orange River</a><sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dowsett_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dowsett-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Irwin_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irwin-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In South Africa, steppe eagles are reportedly often frequent only in the <a href="/wiki/Veld" title="Veld">lowveld</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kruger_National_Park" title="Kruger National Park">Kruger National Park</a> area.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle's wintering range also extends into the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>. They occur broadly in the season in several central and southern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a> as well as regularly in eastern <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and western <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> with odd ones north to <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkey (country)">Turkey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Al-Sheikhly_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Sheikhly-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abuladze_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abuladze-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Although sometimes recorded as occurring "somewhat" in Arabia, more extensive surveying has revealed that many, if not more, steppe eagles wind up winter in the peninsula rather than Africa, and that the largest ever winter numbers were recorded in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, where around 7200 individuals (or perhaps up to 9% of the current world population) were recorded near <a href="/wiki/Riyadh_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Riyadh Region">Riyadh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Keijmel_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keijmel-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> As many as 3000 have also been similarly recorded in the nation of <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Keijmel_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keijmel-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Other nations to host wintering steppe eagles include <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> as well as, albeit rarely doing so, in the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Unusually, a few overwintering steppe eagles have been now recorded in <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, apparently near <a href="/wiki/Shymkent" title="Shymkent">Shymkent</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Aksu-Zhabagly_Nature_Reserve" title="Aksu-Zhabagly Nature Reserve">Aksu-Zhabagly Nature Reserve</a>, the valley of the <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syr Darya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chardara_Dam" title="Chardara Dam">Chardara Dam</a> and towns of the <a href="/wiki/East_Kazakhstan_Region" title="East Kazakhstan Region">East Kazakhstan Region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gennadievich_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gennadievich-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nikolaevich_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nikolaevich-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">south Asia</a>, the species in winter may occur from <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (rarely wintering still in the <a href="/wiki/Nuristan_Province" title="Nuristan Province">Nuristan Province</a>) and in much of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Poonch_District,_Pakistan" title="Poonch District, Pakistan">Poonch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jhelum_District" title="Jhelum District">Jhelum valleys</a> of <a href="/wiki/Azad_Kashmir" title="Azad Kashmir">Azad Kashmir</a> are known to host a mean of 154 steppe eagles per study area.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In India, they may occur mainly south to <a href="/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh" title="Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain" title="Indo-Gangetic Plain">Indo-Gangetic Plain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Deccan Peninsula">Deccan Peninsula</a> and Himalayan zone, <a href="/wiki/Mizoram" title="Mizoram">Mizoram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Orissa" class="mw-redirect" title="Orissa">Orissa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sashi-Kumar_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sashi-Kumar-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Vagrants have been recorded in India to <a href="/wiki/Periyar_National_Park" title="Periyar National Park">Periyar National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahendragiri,_Tamil_Nadu" title="Mahendragiri, Tamil Nadu">Mahendragiri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanyakumari_Wildlife_Sanctuary" title="Kanyakumari Wildlife Sanctuary">Kanyakumari Wildlife Sanctuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mudumalai_National_Park" title="Mudumalai National Park">Mudumalai National Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The wintering range extends east to <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> (although the species is said to be gone from <a href="/wiki/Lhasa" title="Lhasa">Lhasa</a> in recent years), <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a> and broadly in <a href="/wiki/East_China" title="East China">east China</a> from southeastern <a href="/wiki/Guizhou" title="Guizhou">Guizhou</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a> and southwestern <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Recent wintering records reflect the species as lingering seasonally at different points of the non-breeding season, albeit very seldomly, in central and southern <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>, western <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, peninsular <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Duckworth_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Duckworth-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The species may have been aided in expanding their eastward wintering range by <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a> practice.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis)_(32675989348).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2832675989348%29.jpg/220px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2832675989348%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2832675989348%29.jpg/330px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2832675989348%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2832675989348%29.jpg/440px-Steppe_Eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29_%2832675989348%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="2405" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_Eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis)_(32675989348).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A young steppe eagle seen in <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migratory_range">Migratory range</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Migratory range">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The steppe eagle appears broadly in many nations between their central Eurasian breeding areas and their generally tropical Indo and African wintering grounds. As a matter of fact, the largest concentrations of the species tend to occur at times of passage.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The steppe eagle can also vagrate not infrequently far away from traditional migration sites, and has turned up in many areas from <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western Europe</a> to as far east as <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Vagrant steppe eagles have been recorded in at least the following nations or regions: at least 6 nations in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">west Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> (at least 50 times) as well as <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> (in both of which they once bred but were extirpated),<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mordovia" title="Mordovia">Mordovia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yakutia" class="mw-redirect" title="Yakutia">Yakutia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a><sup id="cite_ref-Modern_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Modern-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and probably down to <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">Borneo</a> in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-Duckworth_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Duckworth-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Migration sites include both mountainous ridges and the larger seas along their routes. Steppe eagles predominantly use two main migration routes: one radiates across the Middle East and Arabia, with many birds stopping to winter, but many too migrate around the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> to winter in Africa while the other main migration path frequently involves farther eastern breeding eagles moving along many ridges and prominent flyways before radiated across a broad path through the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>, in order to reach the <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">south Asian</a> and other Asian wintering sites. Less known or less frequently migration paths before these well-known routes of passage may lead steppe eagles around the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> in the west and, much more frequently, around the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> farther east. Nations known to be visited by steppe eagles almost exclusively in migratory passage include <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, most but not all of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and much of east China from <a href="/wiki/Tuquan_County" title="Tuquan County">Tuquan County</a> to about <a href="/wiki/Xiamen" title="Xiamen">Xiamen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IUCN_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IUCN-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Points of migration bottleneck, where large numbers of steppe eagles are frequently recorded, are known in areas including <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, especially around <a href="/wiki/Eilat" title="Eilat">Eilat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suez" title="Suez">Suez</a> (in Egypt), <a href="/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb" title="Bab-el-Mandeb">Bab-el-Mandeb</a> (in Yemen), some parts of the nation of Georgia and, in the Himalayan region, especially within Nepal but also sometimes en masse in Pakistan and <a href="/wiki/Northern_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern India">northern India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Migration sites of minor significance are less known but include <a href="/wiki/Alborz" title="Alborz">Alborz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habitat">Habitat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Habitat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg/220px-Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg/330px-Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg/440px-Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_of_western_Kazakhstan_in_the_early_spring.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The vast and quite flat steppe is the unique home of breeding steppe eagles.</div></div></div>
<p>The steppe eagle tends to breeds in open dry country, within the characteristic habitat it is named after: the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> both in both upland and lowland areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In Kazakhstan, it is known to generally occur in drier parts of the steppe than some other raptors like <a href="/wiki/Harrier_(bird)" title="Harrier (bird)">harriers</a>. This species generally avoids utilizing <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_land" title="Agricultural land">agricultural land</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arables</a> and most other <a href="/wiki/Habitat_fragmentation" title="Habitat fragmentation">human-fragmented areas</a>, however, they can be somewhat tolerant of nesting near roads.<sup id="cite_ref-Sanchez-Zapata_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanchez-Zapata-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wassink_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wassink-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Associated habitats are frequented when breeding such as flat <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a>, arid <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grassland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-desert</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert edge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Most members of the species breed at lower levels but largely in eastern part of the range also will nest in poorly vegetated dry <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">rocky</a> <a href="/wiki/Hill" title="Hill">hillsides</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">massifs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upland_and_lowland" title="Upland and lowland">upland</a> valleys, though generally avoid truly <a href="/wiki/Montane_ecosystems" title="Montane ecosystems">mountainous areas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wassink_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wassink-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Wintering steppe eagles often occur much more frequently in human-modified areas in order to access easy foods. These include <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> <a href="/wiki/Carrion" title="Carrion">carcass</a> dumps, these being used frequently everywhere from Arabia to India.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> More natural habitats used most often by wintering steppe eagles tend to various <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Waterway" title="Waterway">waterways</a> where they are available.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In winter, mostly <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> are the predominant habitat used in Africa, also sometimes <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_dry_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical dry broadleaf forests">dry woodland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steyn_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steyn-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Study in Botswana indicated that wintering steppe eagles there appeared to be indifferent to <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a> changes by humans.<sup id="cite_ref-Herremans_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herremans-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, it was found that the steppe eagle was only frequent in high-elevation <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> areas from 370 to 2,400&#160;m (1,210 to 7,870&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres above sea level">metres above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dowsett_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dowsett-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Use of plateaus was also frequent in Zimbabwe, often where open savanna woods of <i><a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">Acacia</a></i> stand as well as the use of cultivated areas such as <a href="/wiki/Crop_residue" title="Crop residue">wheat stubble fields</a> by eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-Irwin_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irwin-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Iraqi wintering steppe eagles often used <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">dump sites</a> as well as deserts and semi-arid areas, with more steppe, other grassland and mountain slopes used in northern Iraq in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-Al-Sheikhly_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Sheikhly-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> steppe eagles are apparently frequent in old <a href="/wiki/Field_(agriculture)" title="Field (agriculture)">fields</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orchard" title="Orchard">orchards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Adamian_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adamian-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">south Asia</a> they usually use <a href="/wiki/Open_terrain" title="Open terrain">open country</a> and often frequents large <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lakes</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> near arid areas but may accept, or even prefer, more heavily <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">wooded areas</a> (however the first records from peninsular <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> seem to be from open areas created by deforestation).<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ali_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ali-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Although usually a breeder of lowlands, it has been known to live at elevations of up to 2,300&#160;m (7,500&#160;ft) and locally to 3,000&#160;m (9,800&#160;ft) in mountains, on passage can occur to over 4,500&#160;m (14,800&#160;ft) sometimes even to 7,925&#160;m (26,001&#160;ft), as was recorded on <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson-Lees_2-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-Lees-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Compared to other <a href="/wiki/Palearctic" class="mw-redirect" title="Palearctic">Palearctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">migrating</a> eagles, the steppe eagle seems to perhaps be slightly more tolerant of a wider range of <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climatic conditions</a>, including rather <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humid</a> conditions in India provided subsistence is available as well as up to 50&#160;cm (20&#160;in) of snow cover in Kazakhstan (living off of urban <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Nikolaevich_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nikolaevich-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kataria_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kataria-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Behaviour">Behaviour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Steppe_eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Behaviour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Steppe_eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29.jpg/220px-Steppe_eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Steppe_eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29.jpg/330px-Steppe_eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Steppe_eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29.jpg/440px-Steppe_eagle_%28Aquila_nipalensis%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steppe_eagle_(Aquila_nipalensis).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A steppe eagle juvenile seen in <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>.</div></div></div>
