<p>The nomadic nature of steppe eagles in winter can make accurate counts of the species in that season difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-Naoroji_12-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naoroji-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> However, the species is still considered relatively frequent during winter in Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Declines from migrating and wintering areas appear to be generally poorly documented.<sup id="cite_ref-GPS_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPS-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> There is concern that <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a> function as <a href="/wiki/Ecological_trap" title="Ecological trap">ecological traps</a> for these species, due to poisoning being frequent and powerlines frequently a present threat.<sup id="cite_ref-GPS_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GPS-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> From the years 1882 to 2013, an estimated 76,879 steppes were recorded in 9 countries in Indian subcontinent, including Afghanistan, Pakistan, Nepal, Tibet, Bhutan, Sikkim, Myanmar and Bangladesh, often gathering around garbage and carrion dumps.<sup id="cite_ref-Pande_171-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pande-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> They may be even locally increasing somewhat in number in locales in India such as <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, possibly concentrated more so due to less competition from vultures.<sup id="cite_ref-Sashi-Kumar_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sashi-Kumar-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> However, toxic levels of <a href="/wiki/Diclofenac" title="Diclofenac">diclofenac</a> were found in two dead steppe eagles at the cattle carcass dump in <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a>. A paper based on joint research conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Natural_History_Society" title="Bombay Natural History Society">Bombay Natural History Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_for_the_Protection_of_Birds" title="Royal Society for the Protection of Birds">Royal Society for the Protection of Birds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Veterinary_Research_Institute" title="Indian Veterinary Research Institute">Indian Veterinary Research Institute</a>, published in May 2014 in the journal of the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Press" title="Cambridge University Press">Cambridge University Press</a>, highlighted that steppe eagles are adversely affected by <a href="/wiki/Diclofenac" title="Diclofenac">diclofenac</a> and may fall prey to veterinary use of it. The research found the same signs of kidney failure as seen in the <i><a href="/wiki/Gyps" title="Gyps">Gyps</a></i> vulture killed due to diclofenac. They found extensive visceral gout, lesions and uric acid deposits in the liver, kidney and spleen, as well as deposits of diclofenac residue in tissues. Steppe eagles are opportunistic scavengers, which may expose them to the risk of diclofenac poisoning.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Phadnis2014_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phadnis2014-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> Declines have pronounced in passage at Eilat, Israel, where the number of steppe eagle juveniles to adult has dropped 30% from the early 1980s and by 1.4% by 2000; all record low annual numbers in migration there have been subsequent to the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Yosef_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yosef-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yosef2_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yosef2-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> However, lower numbers in Eilat may be due in part to increasingly large portions of the steppe eagle population now wintering in Arabia rather than Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Persecution of raptors in Eilat appears to be still quite prevalent, with steppe eagles accounting for 9.1% of 77 raptors that were found killed by poachers (often appeared to been wrapped in rope and sometimes mutilated), doing so apparently largely out of <a href="/wiki/Superstition" title="Superstition">superstition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Some population declines of migrants in Israel may too have depleted as well by the <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl disaster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yosef_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yosef-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yosef2_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yosef2-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Israeli biologist have strongly advocated that stricter protection be undertaken and a conserved greenbelt be instituted to accommodate the steppe eagle and other raptors in passage.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The similar numbers seen in passage exiting Africa in spring as those entering in autumn indicate that mortality for the species is not high in that continent.<sup id="cite_ref-Weiss_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weiss-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Persecution through shooting likely continues to be of determent to steppe eagles migrating or wintering in the countries of Georgia, Armenia, Iraq and Jordan, with the eagles being relatively vulnerable due to their sluggish, unwary demeanor and, in Iraq, along with many raptors end up being offered at local markets.<sup id="cite_ref-Adamian_102-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adamian-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Al-Sheikhly_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Sheikhly-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, the turnover to more intensive farming activity has depleted to available habitat usable for steppe eagles.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> In Saudi Arabia as well as Iraq and Armenia, other conservation concerns are similar as elsewhere, including dangerous powerlines and potential poisonings.<sup id="cite_ref-Keijmel_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keijmel-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Helbig-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Helbig_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Helbig_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Helbig_3-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Helbig, A. <li id="cite_note-Clark-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Clark_4-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFClark1992" class="citation journal cs1">Clark, W.S.
